        <p class="date">
         Wed Feb 04, 2015 at 10:34 AM PST
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2015/02/04/1362281/-Creationist-theme-park-planners-to-sue-state-for-not-giving-them-free-money" id="titleHref">
          Creationist theme park planners to sue state for not giving them free money
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Hunter">
          Hunter
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=1054&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2015/02/04/1362281/-Creationist-theme-park-planners-to-sue-state-for-not-giving-them-free-money" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="Creationist theme park planners to sue state for not giving them free money" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2015/02/04/1362281/-Creationist-theme-park-planners-to-sue-state-for-not-giving-them-free-money" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="219" data-story_id="1362281" href="/story/2015/02/04/1362281/-Creationist-theme-park-planners-to-sue-state-for-not-giving-them-free-money#comments">
           219 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <span class="image_container">
           <img alt="Noah's Ark" defang_height="" defang_width="" src="http://images.dailykos.com/images/1558/large/dreamstime_s_4948839.jpg?1342729830"/>
          </span>
          <div class="dkimg-cap">
           It'll have two of every animal and the smell will be atrocious.
          </div>
         </div>
         In Kentucky, creationist Ken Ham is attempting to build a new theme park. It will be called Ark Encounter, and will feature a full-sized Noah's Ark, and will feature as a "theme" the notion that you can believe in the absolute literalism of every bit of the one book of the Old Testament that Ken Ham personally gives a damn about or you can go right to Hell, you monster, you.
         <p>
          Those of you who are avid followers of Old Testament theme park construction updates will no doubt have heard, however, that the park plans have run into a considerable snag. The state of Kentucky was going to fund the new mini-monstrosity to the tune of $18 million in tax incentives, but those incentives got cancelled because the theme park planners demanded the right to discriminate when staffing the park. You can almost always get a state to throw money your way to build a new state attraction, but it's another thing to propose that the state give you $18 million in free money and carve out a special exception for you so that you don't have to follow anti-discrimination laws when you're doing it.
         </p>
         <p>
          Now Ken Ham is doing the only logical Old Testament Christian thing. He's gonna sue their asses off
          <a href="http://talkingpointsmemo.com/livewire/ark-encounter-kentucky-discrimination-suit">
           for not letting him discriminate
          </a>
          .
          <br/>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "Our organization spent many months attempting to reason with state officials so that this lawsuit would not be necessary," Answers in Genesis President Ken Ham said in the statement. "However, the state was so insistent on treating our religious entity as a second-class citizen that we were simply left with no alternative but to proceed to court. This is the latest example of increasing government hostility towards religion in America, and it's certainly among the most blatant."
         </blockquote>
         To repeat, Ken Ham is suing because he won't get his pork. To repeat more accurately, Ken Ham is suing
         <em>
          not
         </em>
         because the state will not let him impose a potential religious test for the people who are going to work the burger stands at his new park, but because
         <em>
          the state has refused to give him bagfuls of free money to do it
         </em>
         . That is an outrage, because ignorant backwoods-creationist blowhards who build museums devoted to the premise that Jesus taught man how to properly saddle and ride dinosaurs need to be paid free taxpayer moneys to build new crappy Ned Flanders-inspired theme park slash petting zoos slash outdoor religious meth labs or America is not America anymore. If Ken Ham is not allowed to discriminate while building things on the taxpayer's dime, isn't he the real victim here?
         <p>
          No. No he is not. And if the good Old Testament Christians of America cannot come up with the money to open their own personal theme park with Noah's Arks and petting zoos and flagrant religious discrimination as God intended they have only themselves to blame.
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>

           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>
        </div>

               <p>
                One phrase comes to mind...
                <br/>
                "Praise the Lord and pass the ammunition".
               </p>
               <p>
                Hmm, religion is first after all. It's just a perversion of what the faith actually says.
                <br/>
                But then, Jesus did tell Peter to sell his cloak to get a sword. Then chastised him for using the fucking thing. Screw all if I can figure that stupidity out.
                <br/>
                Oh wait, Jesus was able to tell the future and know that if Peter didn't have a sword, he couldn't forgive the arresting officer. Or something. ;)
               </p>
               <p>
                Do you know one thing that Catholic school can do? Turn one into one hell of a weapon against an entire multi-sect religion.
                <br/>
                And yes, I do indeed like sects. The more, the better.
                <br/>
                Other than the pun, it is indeed more fun. Turning handfuls at a time away from their faith is fun. Doing so individually is far too easy.
                <br/>
                Though, I'll admit, Witlesses are a bit more challenging to do with any other sect. But, individually and later in groups, still fun. They've finally stopped coming to my door, they started running low on elders.
               </p>

             </span>

            <p>
             He used "teenage dinosaurs"
             <br/>
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             <strong>
              How Did Those Huge Dinosaurs Fit on the Ark?
             </strong>
             <br/>
             Although there are about 668 names of dinosaurs, there are perhaps only 55 different kinds of dinosaurs. Furthermore, not all dinosaurs were huge like the brachiosaurus, and even those dinosaurs on the Ark were probably teenagers or young adults.
            </blockquote>
            <blockquote>
             According to Genesis 6:15 , the Ark measured 300 x 50 x 30 cubits, which is about 510 x 85 x 51 feet, with a volume of about 2.21 million cubic feet. Researchers have shown that this is the equivalent volume of over 500 semitrailers of space. 1
             <p>
              Without getting into all the math, the 16,000-plus animals would have occupied much less than half the space in the Ark (even allowing them some moving-around space).
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <a href="https://answersingenesis.org/dinosaurs/were-dinosaurs-on-noahs-ark/">
             https://answersingenesis.org/...

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              16,000 animals was all they took along? So that means something like 8000 different species, by my estimates.
             </p>
             <p>
              I'm no zoologist, but how many species of land animal are there on Earth? Seconds of internet research yield an array of answers between about 900,000 and several million.
             </p>
             <p>
              So here's my question Ham Job: Assuming the low end of that scale, where did the other 892,000 species of land animal come from if they weren't on the Ark? Did they arrive from other planets in the universe? Was it (da-da-dahhhhhh)
              <em>
               evolution???
              </em>
             </p>
             <p>
              And I'll leave it to those better versed in engineering to explain why you couldn't have used all 2.21 million cubic feet of absolute volume as "passenger" space.

            screeching halt to this monument to the creepy inner mind of Ken Ham, is a modern day, and biblically inspired, Herodias; a Jessica Hahn with ambition, if you will.

               </p>
               <blockquote>
                <a href="http://www.holysmoke.org/cretins/fludmath.htm">
                 The math of "Noah's Flood"
                </a>
                <br/>
                The temperature would thusly rise 1800 K, or 1,526.84 C (that's 2,780.33 F...lead melts at 880 F...ed note). It would be highly unlikely that anything short of fused quartz would survive such an onslaught. Also, the water level would have to rise at an average rate of 5.5 inches/min; and in 13 minutes would be in excess of 6' deep.
                <p>
                 Finally, at 1800 K water would not exist as liquid.
                </p>
                <p>
                 It is quite clear that a Biblical Flood is and was quite impossible. Only fools and those shackled by dogma would insist otherwise.

           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            I was always curious...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1362281/55580018#c69?mode=alone;showrate=1#c69">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:918758">
              thanatokephaloides
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:641606">
              Dodgerdog1
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            There are plenty of animals that can live without land. What happened to those during "the flood"? I'm talking about a whole bunch of birds, reptiles, mammals, insects... Not just the fully aquatic ones, but some semi-aquatic animals would do fine.
           </p>
           <p>
            Plus smaller animals could survive on various flotsam that would inevitably be abundant had the whole planet flooded. Heck, even people could survive on an impromptu floating raft (i.e. a bunch of uprooted trees) for 40 days without supplies. It's pretty tough, but it's been done in modern times.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'm sure the creationists have some kind of rebuttal for this - anyone know what it is?
           </p>

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I'm no great supporter of Answers in Genesis, but am in favor of honesty in criticism. The question is not money to build the theme park, but a partial rebate of sales tax it takes in once it is operating. The state offers this to encourage tourist attractions because they are still getting more tax money than if the park wasn't operating. For the more liberal types, who believe in hearing both sides of an argument before issuing condemnations, you can read AIG's defense of the lawsuit at
            <a href="https://answersingenesis.org/religious-freedom/aig-file-discrimination-suit-against-kentucky/">

           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            God told Noah to take one pair of ritually unclean animals and seven pairs of ritually clean animals aboard the ark. The flood story is in Genesis. God tells Moses how to tell clean from unclean animals in Leviticus.
           </p>

        <li id="c201">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55606111">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Question for the Inerrancy Crowd
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1362281/55606111#c201?mode=alone;showrate=1#c201">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>

           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            God told Moses to take one pair of ritually clean animals and seven pairs of ritually clean animals aboard the ark. The flood story is in Genesis.
           </p>
           <p>
            God doesn't specify what makes an animal clean or unclean until he tells Moses.  That story is in Leviticus, chronologically a couple of thousand years after the flood.
           </p>
           <p>
            So how could Noah know which animals are clean and which are unclean?
           </p>

        <li id="c210">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55612456">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            I grew up on Bible stories.
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1362281/55612456#c210?mode=alone;showrate=1#c210">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Somehow I always knew that is what they were stories written by people (excuse me men). I thought they were there to make a point and were not recorded history.
           </p>
           <p>
            No one ever showed me the original in God's handwriting or even that of Jesus.
           </p>
           <p>
            Why are these "Christians" so obsessed with the Old Testament anyway? Do they know He was not born yet?
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:979317">
             TNNurse
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1362281/55612456#c210">
             Sun Feb 08, 2015 at 10:07:16 AM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <li id="c212">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55617049">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Religious Whack-O's 101
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1362281/55617049#c212?mode=alone;showrate=1#c212">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Jesus? Are you there? Hey...I just wanted to tell you that if you didn't already know this, but there are all these really stupid morons on this planet who are using your name to put forward their own biased agenda.
           </p>
           <p>
            You know...for centuries now, many of these religious whack-o's have repeatedly predicted your return, of which...they have been repeatedly WRONG time after time. So...since I know and YOU know that you're really not coming back...ever...I was wondering if you had the power to at least shut these dumbasses up. 'Cause I'm getting really sick and tired of these worthless, mindless and useless religious twits pushing their bullshit agenda and unfounded and unproven beliefs on everyone else.
           </p>
           <p>
            Whaddaya think Jesus? Can you help those of us non-believers down here deal with your blind, ignorant, arrogant followers finally by, I don't know...maybe taking them all early (and permanently thank you) so we can get on with our lives already?
           </p>
           <p>
            SIN-cerely,
           </p>
           <p>
            A normal human being with common sense.
           </p>
          </div>

           <p class="sig">

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
